<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/templates/jsp/pb2/js/plugin/thiss-ds.js" nonce="4d774c8faf334511a00664a29e92e7e4"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="4d774c8faf334511a00664a29e92e7e4">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: '0fd3ddb9-2232-44e5-882e-a18175f6a2a3'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

        (function() {
            function riskifiedBeaconLoad() {
                var store_domain = 'https://advanced.onlinelibrary.wiley.com';
                var session_id = '85FB24BE3B092DE4100D40BE222A29A8';

                s.src = url;

                x.parentNode.insertBefore(s, x);
            }

                window.attachEvent('onload', riskifiedBeaconLoad)
            else

Toward Sodium Dual-Ion Batteries link" href="https://doi.org/10.1002/adfm.202414761">https://doi.org/10.1002/adfm.202414761</a></div></div><span class="openUrl"><a    <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d435183107" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>To achieve high-quality hard carbon nanofibers (HCNFs), and particularly flexible HCNFs films is the eternal pursuit from low-cost coal pitch (CP). However, it is still trapped seriously by the inborn bottleneck of low-softening-point (LSP) characteristics of CP itself. Herein, an efficient Bi(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>·5H<sub>2</sub>O-assisted electrospinning-carbonization methodology is creatively devised to obtain flexible HCNFs films directly from LSP CP. The essential roles of Bi(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>·5H<sub>2</sub>O and pre-oxidation in constructing flexible films are rationally proposed. With further regulation in Bi(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>·5H<sub>2</sub>O dosage and calcination temperatures, specific micro-structures/morphologies of flexible HCNFs films are finely optimized. The optimum HCNFs-1.2 film is endowed with robust structural flexibility/stability, high-content active oxygen/nitrogen groups, abundant graphic microcrystalline zones of large interlayer spacing, and convenient ion-diffusion channels. Thanks to such remarkable merits, HCNFs-1.2 retains a large reversible capacity of 125.3 mAh g<sup>‒1</sup> over 1000 cycles at 1.0 A g<sup>‒1</sup>, when evaluated as a self-supporting film anode for sodium dual-ion batteries (SDIBs). Furthermore, the HCNFs-1.2-based SDIBs deliver a specific capacity of 90.9 mAh g<sup>‒1</sup> at 0.1 A g<sup>‒1</sup>, along with a capacity retention of 78.4% after 1500 cycles at 1.0 A g<sup>‒1</sup>. The insightful understanding here will provide meaningful guidance for rational design of advanced flexible film electrodes toward next-generation SDIBs and beyond.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202414761-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202414761-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>The large-scale and continuous utilization of renewable energy induces the contradiction between the uneven spatial and temporal distributions of energy supply, which makes the development of efficient energy storage devices more imminent.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0001_R_d435183099e414" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Nano Energy">1</a>, <a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0002_R_d435183099e414" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">2</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Recently, electrochemical energy storage devices, especially lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), have attracted extensive attention due to their high energy density and long cycle life.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0003_R_d435183099e419" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Electrochim. Acta.">3</a>, <a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0004_R_d435183099e419" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, in the face of the severe situation of lithium resource shortage and uneven distribution, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have become the first choice as the large-scale energy storage technology due to its low cost and abundant natural resources.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0005_R_d435183099e424" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - ChemElectroChem">5</a>, <a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0006_R_d435183099e424" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Adv. Mater.">6</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Compared to SIBs, sodium dual-ion batteries (SDIBs), which use the commercial graphite materials as a positive electrode, which can further effectively reduce the cost.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0007_R_d435183099e430" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, SDIBs, as a pioneering and alternative energy storage technology with the appealing advantages including wide voltage windows, low cost, high safety, and high energy density, have been becoming a research hotspot since they were first reported in 2015.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0008_R_d435183099e435" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Energy Mater.">8</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Different from other common metal ion batteries, SDIBs generally utilize the reversible (de)intercalation of anions and cations in the electrolyte from/into the involved cathodes and anodes, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0009_R_d435183099e441" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Adv. Energy Mater.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> It is well known that anions can be inserted/de-inserted from the graphite cathode at high operation potentials (&gt;4.5&nbsp;V vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na), which thus increases the operating voltage and energy density of the devices.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0010_R_d435183099e448" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Chem. Eng. J.">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Unfortunately, as regards SDIBs, there is still an enormous challenge of how to develop high-performance anode candidates with appropriate micro-structures to efficiently accommodate Na<sup>+</sup> with even larger size of 1.06 Å.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0011_R_d435183099e456" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - J. Mater. Chem. A.">11</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Hard carbon (HC) materials are considered to be the most anode materials for sodium storage due to their unique merits like rich carbon sources, cost efficiency, non-toxicity, environmental friendliness, and low sodium storage potential.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0012_R_d435183099e463" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Energy Environ. Sci.">12</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Common matrix precursors including biomass, polymers, and resins are well explored to produce HC materials.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0013_R_d435183099e468" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Mater. Today">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Nevertheless, the high-cost efficiency and low carbon yield of these precursors limit their practical applications in electrochemical sodium storage. Besides, 1D porous HC nanofibers (HCNFs) are emerging as a competitive anode for sodium storage benefiting from their unique micro-structures, providing abundant electroactive sites and short diffusion/transmission path for both ions and electrons.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0014_R_d435183099e473" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - J. Anal. Appl. Pyrol.">14</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Furthermore, the HCNFs-constructed self-standing fiber films have been explored intensively and further utilized directly as a flexible self-supported electrode for sodium storage, which avoids the use of polymeric binders, conductive additives, and even current collectors, enormously simplifying the preparation procedure and enhancing energy density of devices.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0015_R_d435183099e479" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">15</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> More significantly, the film electrodes will make the flexible cells meet the special requirements for the wearable, bendable, and implantable electronic devices.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0016_R_d435183099e484" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Adv. Fiber Mater.">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As a consequence, it is highly meaningful yet an enormous challenge to explore certain low-cost, high-carbon-content natural carbon sources toward simple fabrication of high-quality HCNFs film electrode with remarkable sodium-storage capability meanwhile.</p>
         
         <p>Recently, the pitch products have drawn much attention as an extremely cheap but high-carbon-content precursor for HC synthesis. However, the low-softening-point (LSP) feature of the commercial pitch seriously restrains its applications in fine preparation of HCNFs, let alone flexible nano-fibrous films.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0017_R_d435183099e492" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - J. Enegry Chem.">17</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The underlying reasons for this mainly lie on the fact that the HCNFs prepared directly from the LSP pitch will spontaneously soften and melt when carbonized at high calcination temperatures, and cannot maintain the typical fibrous morphology at all.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0018_R_d435183099e497" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Adv. Energy Mater.">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To well address such issues, it is highly necessary to carry out non-melting treatment before carbonization to make it change from thermoplastic material to thermosetting one, which ensures that the pitch-derived HCNFs will not melt during carbonization. Besides this, it should not be ignored as well that the strong π-π interaction between pitch molecules, mainly polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbons, makes it easy to graphitize.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0019_R_d435183099e502" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Chem. Rec.">19</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> During the high-temperature carbonization process, the pitch molecules will re-arrange to form parallel stacked carbon sheets with few defects and high graphitization degree.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0018_R_d435183099e508" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Adv. Energy Mater.">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Therefore, further scientific regulation of the micro-structures of pitch-based HCNFs will favors the enhancement in the Na<sup>+</sup>-storage performance, which can not only realizes the high value-added utilization of commercial pitch, but also promotes the practicality of pitch-derived anodes-based SDIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0020_R_d435183099e515" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Chem. Rev.">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>So far, two main avenues, i.e., increasing the softening point of pitch by high temperature/pressure thermal polycondensation or thermal polymerization, and exploring an alternative non-melting condition, have been generally established.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0021_R_d435183099e522" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Carbon">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In general, the former has been widely used, but it has the problems of complex preparation process and high cost, and the latter is commonly realized via the non-melting treatment of pitch in different oxidation media including NO<sub>2</sub>, O<sub>2</sub>, air, halogen gas, and other strong oxidation reagents.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0014_R_d435183099e531" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - J. Anal. Appl. Pyrol.">14</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As early as 2000, Thomas et al.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0022_R_d435183099e537" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Electrochim. Acta">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> investigated the mesophase asphalt-based carbon fibers P75 and P100 as SIBs anodes. The obtained carbon fibers with micrometer diameter and layer spacing of ≈0.34&nbsp;nm showed poor sodium storage performance just with a maximum reversible capacity of ≈83 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 7&nbsp;µA mg<sup>−1</sup>. Therefore, proper structural regulation is the key to improve the performance of bituminous carbon fibers for storing sodium. For instance, Qiu et al.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0023_R_d435183099e547" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Carbon">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> mixed the polyacrylonitrile with LSP coal pitch (CP) and then use it to electrospin flexible carbon nanofibers (CNFs) with the air pre-oxidation and high-temperature ammonia treatment. Our group once developed electrospinning strategy to obtain CNFs through concentrated nitric acid pretreatment of LSP pitch, well solving the instability issue of nanofibers.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0024_R_d435183099e552" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Rare Met.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the interlayer spacings of as-achieved HCNFs are relatively small along with the few defect sites, which makes it not suitable for Na<sup>+</sup> storage. Analogously, Li et al.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0025_R_d435183099e559" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Energ. Fuel.">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> used coal liquefaction residue as raw material, and prepared nano carbon fiber non-woven fabrics as independent electrodes through HNO<sub>3</sub> pre-oxidation, air stabilization and carbonization. Accordingly, it will be an enormous breakthrough to develop a low-cost, and even milder yet efficient methodology for large-scale fabrication of flexible HCNFs films, particularly with striking sodium-storage properties.</p>
         
         <p>In this work, to the best of our knowledge, we first devised a Bi(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>·5H<sub>2</sub>O-assisted electrospinning-calcination avenue to controllably produce 3D porous HCNFs flexible films by using the commercial LSP CP as the carbon precursor, and the low-carbonization-rate polyvinylpyrrolidone (PVP) as a spinning assistant. The intrinsic role of Bi(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>·5H<sub>2</sub>O in the construction of porous HCNFs flexible films was rationally put forward as well as the contribution from pre-oxidation. With comprehensive regulations in both Bi(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>·5H<sub>2</sub>O content and calcination temperatures, specific micro-structures of porous HCNFs in terms of porosity, surface functional groups, graphite microcrystalline structure, and interlayer spacings were purposefully optimized. The optimal HCNFs film was endowed with excellent mechanical flexibility, robust structural stability, porous structure, and large interlayer spacing, and exhibited a capacity of 238.4 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.05 A g<sup>‒1</sup>, along with a striking electrochemical stability (a capacity retention of ≈87.3% over 1000 cycles at 1.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>), when evaluated for sodium storage as the self-supporting anode. After assembled with the commercial graphite cathode, the sodium dual-ion batteries (SDIBs) were constructed, and gained reversible capacities of 90.9/47.7 mAh g<sup>‒1</sup> at current densities of 0.1/5.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Moreover, the full device retained a capacity retention of 78.4% (equivalent to a mere capacity loss of 0.0144% per cycle) after 1500 consecutive cycles at 1.0 A g<sup>‒1</sup>, highlighting the promising applications of our fabricated flexible HCNFs films for high-performance SDIBs.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202414761-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202414761-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202414761-sec-0030">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adfm202414761-sec-0030-title">2.1 Structural/Physicochemical Analysis of HCNFs-1.2 Films</h3>
            
            <p>Typical synthetic process of HCNFs films is schematically shown in <b>Scheme</b> <a href="#adfm202414761-fig-0009">1</a>. Herein, the Bi(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>·5H<sub>2</sub>O-invloved electrospinning strategy is first designed, along with the carbon source of commercial LSP CP and the spinning assistant of PVP. With following three procedures, i.e., pre-oxidation in air at 230&nbsp;°C, and calcination in Ar at 600 and 1200&nbsp;°C, respectively, the HCNFs films can be successfully fabricated. As visualized in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202414761-fig-0001">1a</a>, the color of electrospun CP-PVP-Bi-1.2 precursor film turns out to be even darker after pre-oxidation, and further black after calcinated under Ar, in which the annealing-induced shrinkage in size clearly occurs. As noted, the achieved HCNFs-1.2 film exhibits superb mechanical flexibility (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202414761-fig-0001">1b</a>), which makes it more suitable as the self-supported electrode. As seen from typical field emission scanning electron microscopy (FESEM) examinations (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202414761-fig-0001">1c,d</a>), the diameter of the achieved HCNFs-1.2 is uniform and estimated as ≈150&nbsp;nm. Besides, the surface of these fibers is relatively rough with several well-discerned bulges, which is supported well by the transmission electron microscopy (TEM) observations (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202414761-fig-0001">1e,f</a>). Evidently, a large number of pores (yellow circles) and a small amount of carbon vesicles (red circles) are evident in and/or on the surface of HCNFs-1.2. Such unique porous architecture should be ascribed to the physical removal of Bi-based species over high-temperature calcination procedure.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0026_R_d435183099e645" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> By analyzing the high-resolution TEM (HRTEM) images and corresponding intensity files (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202414761-fig-0001">1g–i</a>), the abundant short-range graphitic zones with the well-defined interlayer spacings of ≈0.40&nbsp;nm (fiber interior: 0.419&nbsp;nm; vesical: 0.477&nbsp;nm). In general, the large interlayer spacing (&gt;0.37&nbsp;nm) will facilitate the electrochemical storage/release of sodium ions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202414761-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202414761-bib-0027_R_d435183099e653" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Adv. Energy Mater.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Scanning TEM (STEM) and corresponding element mapping images (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202414761-fig-0001">1j</a>) evidence the main existing C species along with a very small amount of evenly distributed N (≈0.3 at.%) in the fibers, and no any Bi signal can be detected, indicating that metallic Bi is completely removed or only contains trace amounts.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202414761-fig-0009"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/15124ed0-be19-4652-964c-1ab850edba23/adfm202414761-fig-0009-m.jpg"><picture>
